<tr>
<th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th>
<td style="line-height:1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gm.com/index.html">www<wbr />.gm<wbr />.com<wbr />/index<wbr />.html</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:1.35em;"><b>Footnotes&#160;/ references</b><br />
<sup id="cite_ref-gm10k2012_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gm10k2012-5">[5]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>General Motors Company</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-filing_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filing-1">[1]</a></sup> commonly known as <b>GM</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, that designs, manufactures, markets, and distributes vehicles and vehicle parts, and sells financial services. With global headquarters at the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Center" title="Renaissance Center">Renaissance Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Detroit,_Michigan" class="mw-redirect" title="Detroit, Michigan">Detroit, Michigan</a>, United States, GM manufactures cars and trucks in 35 countries. In 2008, 8.35 million<sup id="cite_ref-GM_Media_Online_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Media_Online-6">[6]</a></sup> GM cars and trucks were sold globally under various brands. Current auto brands are <a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a>, <a href="/wiki/GMC_(automobile)" title="GMC (automobile)">GMC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">Wuling</a>. Former GM automotive brands include <a href="/wiki/McLaughlin_automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="McLaughlin automobile">McLaughlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland (automobile)">Oakland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oldsmobile" title="Oldsmobile">Oldsmobile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saab_Automobile" title="Saab Automobile">Saab</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Corporation" title="Saturn Corporation">Saturn</a>.</p>
<p>The company was founded by <a href="/wiki/William_C._Durant" title="William C. Durant">William C. Durant</a> on September 16, 1908 as a holding company. The company was the largest automobile manufacturer from 1931 through 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to brands selling assembled vehicles, GM also has had various automotive-component and non-automotive brands, many of which it <a href="/wiki/Divestment" title="Divestment">divested</a> in the 1980s through 2000s. These have included <a href="/wiki/Euclid_Trucks" title="Euclid Trucks">Euclid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terex" title="Terex">Terex</a> (earthmoving/construction/mining equipment &amp; vehicles); <a href="/wiki/Electro-Motive_Diesel" title="Electro-Motive Diesel">Electro-Motive Diesel</a> (locomotive, marine, and industrial <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engines</a>); <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Diesel" title="Detroit Diesel">Detroit Diesel</a> (automotive and industrial diesel engines); <a href="/wiki/Allison_Transmission" title="Allison Transmission">Allison</a> (Aircraft engines,<a href="/wiki/Transmission_(mechanics)" title="Transmission (mechanics)">transmissions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gas_turbine" title="Gas turbine">gas turbine engines</a>); <a href="/wiki/Frigidaire" title="Frigidaire">Frigidaire</a> (Appliances including <a href="/wiki/Refrigeration" title="Refrigeration">refrigeration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a>); New Departure (<a href="/wiki/Bearing_(mechanical)" title="Bearing (mechanical)">bearings</a>); <a href="/wiki/Delco_Electronics" title="Delco Electronics">Delco Electronics</a> and <a href="/wiki/ACDelco" title="ACDelco">ACDelco</a> (electrical and electronic components); <a href="/wiki/Ally_Financial" title="Ally Financial">GMAC</a> (<a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>); <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Aircraft" title="Atlantic Aircraft">General Aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_American_Aviation" title="North American Aviation">North American Aviation</a> (airplanes); <a href="/wiki/GM_Defense" title="GM Defense">GM Defense</a> (military vehicles) and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Data_Systems" title="Electronic Data Systems">Electronic Data Systems</a> (<a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>).</p>
<p>General Motors produces vehicles in 37 countries under twelve brands: <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a>, <a href="/wiki/GMC_(automobile)" title="GMC (automobile)">GMC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holden_Special_Vehicles" title="Holden Special Vehicles">HSV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall_Motors" title="Vauxhall Motors">Vauxhall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wuling_Motors" title="Wuling Motors">Wuling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baojun" title="Baojun">Baojun</a>, <a href="/wiki/FAW-GM" title="FAW-GM">Jie Fang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/GM_Uzbekistan" title="GM Uzbekistan">Ravon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GM_Stockholder-letter_2011_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM_Stockholder-letter_2011-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Our_Company_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Our_Company-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The current company, General Motors Company LLC ("new GM"), was formed in 2009 following the bankruptcy of <b>General Motors Corporation</b> ("old GM"), which became <a href="/wiki/Motors_Liquidation_Company" title="Motors Liquidation Company">Motors Liquidation Company</a>. The new company purchased the majority of the assets of the old GM, including the brand "General Motors".</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_units">Business units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Business units">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In addition to its twelve brands, General Motors also holds a 20% stake in <a href="/wiki/Industries_M%C3%A9caniques_Maghr%C3%A9bines" title="Industries Mécaniques Maghrébines">IMM</a>, and a 77% stake in <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">GM Korea</a>. It also has a number of joint-ventures, including <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_GM" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai GM">Shanghai GM</a>, <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">SAIC-GM-Wuling</a> and <a href="/wiki/FAW-GM" title="FAW-GM">FAW-GM</a> in China, <a href="/wiki/GM-AvtoVAZ" title="GM-AvtoVAZ">GM-AvtoVAZ</a> in Russia, <a href="/wiki/Ghandhara_Industries" title="Ghandhara Industries">Ghandhara Industries</a> in Pakistan, <a href="/wiki/GM_Uzbekistan" title="GM Uzbekistan">GM Uzbekistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_India_Private_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="General Motors India Private Limited">General Motors India</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Egypt" title="General Motors Egypt">General Motors Egypt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Isuzu_Truck_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Isuzu Truck South Africa">Isuzu Truck South Africa</a>. General Motors employs 212,000 people and does business in more than 140 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-GMemploy_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMemploy-2">[2]</a></sup> General Motors is divided into five business segments: <i>GM North America</i> (GMNA), <i><a href="/wiki/Opel_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Opel Group">Opel Group</a></i>, <i>GM International Operations</i> (GMIO), <i>GM South America</i> (GMSA), and <i><a href="/wiki/GM_Financial" title="GM Financial">GM Financial</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-GMannualreport2011_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMannualreport2011-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:12, 13</sup></p>
<p>General Motors led global vehicle sales for 77 consecutive years from 1931 through 2007, longer than any other automaker, and in 2012 was among the world's largest automakers by vehicle unit sales.<sup id="cite_ref-GALLIGAN_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GALLIGAN-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>General Motors acts in most countries outside the U.S. via wholly owned subsidiaries, but operates in <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">China</a> through 10 joint ventures.<sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:18, 96</sup><sup id="cite_ref-GMannualreport2011_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMannualreport2011-11">[11]</a></sup> GM's <a href="/wiki/OnStar" title="OnStar">OnStar</a> subsidiary provides vehicle safety, security and information services.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, General Motors shed several brands, closing <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Corporation" title="Saturn Corporation">Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a>, and emerged from a government-backed <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization" title="General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization">Chapter 11 reorganization</a>. In 2010, the reorganized GM made an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> that was one of the world's top five largest IPOs to date, and returned to profitability later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Businessweek_2012-02-16_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Businessweek_2012-02-16-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_General_Motors" title="History of General Motors">History of General Motors</a></div>
<p>General Motors Corporation was formed on September 16, 1908, in <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint, Michigan</a>, as a <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> controlled by <a href="/wiki/William_C._Durant" title="William C. Durant">William C. Durant</a>, owner of <a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> At the beginning of the 20th century, there were fewer than 8,000 automobiles in America, and Durant had become a leading manufacturer of horse-drawn vehicles in Flint before making his foray into the automotive industry.<sup id="cite_ref-horses_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horses-16">[16]</a></sup> GM's co-founder was <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_Mott" title="Charles Stewart Mott">Charles Stewart Mott</a>, whose carriage company was merged into Buick prior to GM's creation. Over the years, Mott became the largest single stockholder in GM, and spent his life with his <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_Mott_Foundation" title="Charles Stewart Mott Foundation">Mott Foundation</a>, which has benefited the city of Flint, his adopted home. GM acquired <a href="/wiki/Oldsmobile" title="Oldsmobile">Oldsmobile</a> later that year. In 1909, Durant brought in <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elmore_(automobile)" title="Elmore (automobile)">Elmore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland (automobile)">Oakland</a>, and several others. Also in 1909, GM acquired the Reliance Motor Truck Company of <a href="/wiki/Owosso,_Michigan" title="Owosso, Michigan">Owosso, Michigan</a>, and the Rapid Motor Vehicle Company of <a href="/wiki/Pontiac,_Michigan" title="Pontiac, Michigan">Pontiac, Michigan</a>, the predecessors of <a href="/wiki/GMC_(automobile)" title="GMC (automobile)">GMC Truck</a>. Durant, along with R. S. McLaughlin, lost control of GM in 1910 to a bankers' trust, because of the large amount of debt taken on in its acquisitions, coupled with a collapse in new vehicle sales.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg/220px-2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg/330px-2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg/440px-2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1845" data-file-height="1208" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT_--_07-10-2010_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The longest-lived continuous automobile nameplate still in production in the world is the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Suburban" title="Chevrolet Suburban">Chevrolet Suburban</a><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The next year, Durant started the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> Motor Car Company in the U.S., and in Canada in 1915, and through this, he secretly purchased a controlling interest in GM. Durant took back control of the company after one of the most dramatic <a href="/wiki/Proxy_fight" title="Proxy fight">proxy wars</a> in American business history. Durant then reorganized General Motors Company into General Motors Corporation in 1916, merging Chevrolet with GM and merging General Motors of Canada Limited as an ally in 1918. Shortly thereafter, he again lost control, this time for good, after the new vehicle market collapsed. <a href="/wiki/Alfred_P._Sloan" title="Alfred P. Sloan">Alfred P. Sloan</a> was picked to take charge of the corporation, and led it to its post-war global dominance when the seven manufacturing facilities operated by Chevrolet before GM acquired the company began to contribute to GM operations. These facilities were added to the individual factories that were exclusive to Cadillac, Buick, Oldsmobile, Oakland, and other companies acquired by GM. This unprecedented growth of GM would last into the early 1980s, when it employed 349,000 workers and operated 150 assembly plants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chapter_11_bankruptcy">Chapter 11 bankruptcy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Chapter 11 bankruptcy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization" title="General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization">General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization</a></div>
<p>On June 1, 2009, after heavy losses, General Motors went bankrupt. Stockholders lost essentially all of their investment.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:14_Buick_LaCrosse_(14344035480).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg/220px-14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg/330px-14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg/440px-14_Buick_LaCrosse_%2814344035480%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3909" data-file-height="2424" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:14_Buick_LaCrosse_(14344035480).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Buick_LaCrosse#Second_generation_.282010.E2.80.932016.29" title="Buick LaCrosse">2nd generation Buick LaCrosse</a> has been cited as an example of a GM's revival following its restructing in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On July 10, 2009, General Motors emerged from government backed <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 11</a> reorganization after an initial filing on June 8, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-Merced-2009-07-10_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-Merced-2009-07-10-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-Maynard-2009-07-10_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-Maynard-2009-07-10-22">[22]</a></sup> Through the <a href="/wiki/Troubled_Asset_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Asset Relief Program">Troubled Asset Relief Program</a> the US Treasury invested $49.5 billion in General Motors and recovered $39 billion when it sold its shares on December 9, 2013 resulting in a loss of $10.3 billion. The Treasury invested an additional $17.2 billion into GM's former financing company, GMAC (now Ally). The shares in Ally were sold on December 18, 2014 for $19.6 billion netting $2.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto_Industry_Bailout_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto_Industry_Bailout-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-exit_Ally_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exit_Ally-24">[24]</a></sup> A study by the Center for Automotive Research found that the GM bailout saved 1.2 million jobs and preserved $34.9 billion in tax revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Last_Sale_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Last_Sale-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2009 as part General Motors Chapter 11 Bankruptcy, the company shed several brands, closing <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Corporation" title="Saturn Corporation">Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a>, while selling <a href="/wiki/Saab_Automobile" title="Saab Automobile">Saab Automobile</a> to Dutch automaker <a href="/wiki/Spyker_Cars" title="Spyker Cars">Spyker</a>, and emerged from a government-backed <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization" title="General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization">Chapter 11 reorganization</a>. In 2010, the reorganized GM made an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> that was one of the world's top five largest IPOs to date and returned to profitability later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Businessweek_2012-02-16_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Businessweek_2012-02-16-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Corporate governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg/220px-Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg/330px-Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg/440px-Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Detroit_Renaissance-Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Center" title="Renaissance Center">GM World Headquarters</a> in Detroit</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Based on global sales, General Motors is routinely among the world's largest automakers.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Headquartered at the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Center" title="Renaissance Center">Renaissance Center</a> in Detroit, GM employs approximately 202,000 people around the world. In 2009, General Motors sold 6.5&#160;million cars and trucks globally; in 2010, it sold 8.4 million.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of March 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Barra" title="Mary Barra">Mary Barra</a> is the chief executive officer (CEO) and chairman of the board and Daniel Ammann is the president.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The head of design, <a href="/wiki/Edward_T._Welburn" title="Edward T. Welburn">Edward T. Welburn</a>, was the first African American to lead a global automotive design organization, and as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the highest ranking African American in the US motor industry.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>As part of the company's advertising, Ed Whitacre announced the company's 60-day money-back guarantee and repayment of $6.7&#160;billion loan from government ahead of schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> On December 12, 2013, GM announced that Mary Barra, 51, executive vice president, Global Product Development, Purchasing and Supply Chain, was elected by the board of directors to become the next CEO of the company succeeding Dan Akerson on January 15, 2014. Barra also joined the GM board.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> From June 2009 to March 2011, the company had three chief executive officers and three chief financial officers.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_results">Financial results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Financial results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The company has reported annual profits since 2010. It can carry forward previous losses to reduce tax liability on future earnings. It earned $4.7&#160;billion in 2010. The <i>Wall Street Journal</i> estimated the tax break, including credits for costs related to pensions and other expenses can be worth as much as $45&#160;billion over the next 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, General Motors ranked second on the list with 8.5 million units produced globally.<sup id="cite_ref-OICA2010_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OICA2010-37">[37]</a></sup> In 2011, GM returned to the first place with 9.025 million units sold worldwide, corresponding to 11.9% <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of the global motor vehicle industry. The top two markets in 2011 were China, with 2,547,203 units, and the United States, with 2,503,820 vehicles sold. The Chevrolet brand was the main contributor to GM performance, with 4.76 million vehicles sold around the world in 2011, a global sales record.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2011_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2011-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2013 during a commencement speech, CEO Dan Akerson suggested that GM was on the cusp of rejoining the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a> index. GM was removed from the index as it approached bankruptcy in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 24, 2014, <a href="/wiki/CNNMoney" title="CNNMoney">CNNMoney</a> reported that GM profits fell to $108 million for the first three months of 2014. GM now estimates the cost of their <a href="/wiki/2014_General_Motors_recall" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 General Motors recall">2014 recall</a> due to faulty ignition switches, which have been linked to at least 13 deaths, at $1.3 billion. Shares of GM were down 16% for the year before the new announcement of GM's lower profits.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 4, 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> reported that GM led a $1bn equity financing in the transportation network company (TNC) <a href="/wiki/Lyft" title="Lyft">Lyft.com</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> This was GM's first investment in the ride-sharing ecosystem and its reported participation ($500,000,000) in the round is considered to be indicative of its efforts towards the future of driving, which it believes will be "connected, seamless and autonomous".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_Directors">Board of Directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Board of Directors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</div>

<td><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />5.0%</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a filing before the Superior Court of Ontario (Canada), <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Canada" title="General Motors Canada">General Motors Canada</a> is a privately owned Canadian company with the corporation as indirect parent. The employees are not all Canadian, as some salaried personnel are from the U.S. and work for the corporation. GM products focus primarily on its four core divisions&#160;– Chevrolet, Cadillac, Buick, and GMC. The GM restructuring has resulted in a lower break even point for annual sales and renewed profits.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the mid-2005, GM announced that its corporate chrome power emblem "<a href="/wiki/Mark_of_Excellence" title="Mark of Excellence">Mark of Excellence</a>" would begin appearing on all recently introduced and all-new 2006 model vehicles produced and sold in North America. However, in 2009 the "New GM" reversed this, saying that emphasis on its four core divisions would downplay the GM logo.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>GM typically reports as among the largest auto makers in the United States. In May 2012, GM recorded an 18.4% market share in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. </tr>
</table>
<p>In 2008 the third largest individual country by sales was <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_do_Brasil" title="General Motors do Brasil">Brazil</a> with some 550,000 GM vehicles sold. In that year the other South American countries Argentina, Colombia, and Venezuela sold another 300,000 GM vehicles, suggesting that the total GM sales in South America (including sales in other South American countries such as Chile, Peru, Ecuador, Bolivia, etc.) in that year were at a similar level to sales in China.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> is the main GM brand name in Europe except in the United Kingdom, where Opel's British subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall_Motors" title="Vauxhall Motors">Vauxhall</a>, still uses its own "Vauxhall" brand name. The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> brand was reintroduced in Europe in 2005, selling mostly South-Korean made small cars. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Groupe_PSA" title="Groupe PSA">PSA Peugeot Citroen</a> and General Motors formed an alliance, which involved General Motors acquiring seven percent of PSA Group.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 13, 2013, GM announced it had divested itself of its seven percent ownership of PSA Group, generating "gross proceeds of €0.25 billion."<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Also in December 2013, GM announced it would drop the Chevrolet brand in Europe by Q4 2015, to focus on Opel/Vauxhall. Chevrolets will continue to be sold in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>. GM lost approximately $18B over the past 12 years in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Though on 14 February 2017 <a href="/wiki/Groupe_PSA" title="Groupe PSA">Groupe PSA</a> consider in taking over all <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> Business from GM, after GM reported a loss of US$257 millions from its European operations on 2016, sixteenth consecutive loss-making year for GM in Europe, bringing its amount losses on the continent since 2000 to more than US$15 billions.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On 06 March 2017 was confirmed the sell of Opel, Vauxhall and GM Financial due bank BNP Paribas for $2.3 billion. <sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The company manufactures most of its China market vehicles locally. <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_GM" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai GM">Shanghai GM</a>, a joint venture with the Chinese company <a href="/wiki/SAIC_Motor" title="SAIC Motor">SAIC Motor</a>, was created on March 25, 1997. The Shanghai GM plant was officially opened on December 15, 1998, when the first Chinese-built Buick came off the assembly line. The <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile</a> joint-venture is also successfully selling microvans under the <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">Wuling</a> brand (34 percent owned by GM). Much of General Motors' recent growth has been in the People's Republic of China, where its sales rose 66.9 percent in 2009, selling 1,830,000 vehicles and accounting for 13.4 percent of the market.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a> is strong in China, being led by the <a href="/wiki/Buick_Excelle" title="Buick Excelle">Buick Excelle</a> subcompact. The <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">last emperor of China</a> owned a Buick.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a> brand was introduced in China in 2004, starting with exports to China. GM pushed the marketing of the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> brand in China in 2005 as well, transferring <a href="/wiki/Opel_Corsa#Opel_Corsa_B_.281993.E2.80.932000.29" title="Opel Corsa">Buick Sail</a> to that brand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In August 2009 the joint venture of FAW GM Light Duty Commercial Vehicle Co Ltd was formed that mainly produces Jiefang light-duty trucks.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>General Motors vehicle sales in China rose 28.8 percent to a record 2,351,610 units in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> GM set up an auto research center as part of a US250&#160;million corporate campus in Shanghai to develop '<a href="/wiki/Hybrid_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid car">gasoline-hybrid cars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel_vehicle" title="Alternative fuel vehicle">alternative fuels</a>, engines and new technologies'.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The company plans to double its sales from 2010 to about 5 million units in China by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>SAIC-GM-Wuling established the low-cost Baojun brand to better compete with domestic rivals, <a href="/wiki/Chery_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Chery Automobile">Chery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geely_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Geely Automobile">Geely</a> and <a href="/wiki/BYD_Auto" title="BYD Auto">BYD</a> for first-time buyers of cars priced around USD10,000. It is estimated that such market in China is about 5 million vehicles a year, larger than the auto market in France and Britain combined. However, some are worried that 'local brands like Baojun could eventually become threats to their parent brands if they compete more against established models over time'. Shanghai-GM-Wuling sold 1.23 million vehicles in 2010, mainly commercial vans and trucks, of which about 700,000 units were a van called Sunshine.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>GM maintains a dealership presence in Japan, called <a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/GM%E3%82%B7%E3%83%9C%E3%83%AC%E3%83%BC%E5%BA%97" class="extiw" title="ja:GMシボレー店">GM Chevrolet Shop</a>, previously known as <i>GM Auto World Shop</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Current GM Japan dealerships were either former <a href="/wiki/Saturn_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saturn (automobile)">Saturn</a> dealerships or <a href="/wiki/Isuzu" class="mw-redirect" title="Isuzu">Isuzu</a> dealership locations. GM products are also currently sold by the company <a href="/wiki/Yanase_(car_dealership)" title="Yanase (car dealership)">Yanase Co., Ltd.</a> since 1915.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In August 2011, GM announced plans to reactivate its plant that previously produced rebadged Chevrolet Blazer as Opel as well as Brazilian Blazer, and also build a new plant in <a href="/wiki/Bekasi" title="Bekasi">Bekasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>, Indonesia, which would produce 40,000 passenger cars per year for the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Asian">Southeast Asian</a> market. It is the third plant in Southeast Asia, after the <a href="/wiki/Rayong" title="Rayong">Rayong</a> plant, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a> plant, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2011, the South Korea Free Trade Agreement opened up the South Korean auto market to American made cars.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> GM owns (per December 31, 2011) 77.0% of its joint venture in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">GM Korea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GMannualreport2011_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMannualreport2011-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:p.96</sup></p>
<p>On March 11, 2013, GM opened a new 190,300 square-foot manufacturing plant in Bekasi, Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In February 2015, GM announced they will close the Bekasi plant by the end of June and stop production of the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Sonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevrolet Sonic">Sonic</a> in Thailand by mid-year.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG/220px-World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG/330px-World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG/440px-World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:World_locations_of_General_Motors_factories.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Global locations of General Motors' assembly factories.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>GM has a long history in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> which began in the 1920s with the assembly of cars and light pickup trucks for the local market. In the mid of the 1950s, GM withdrew from the Egyptian market. Some years later, the <a href="/wiki/Ghabbour_Group" title="Ghabbour Group">Ghabbour Brothers</a> began to assemble <a href="/wiki/Cadillac" title="Cadillac">Cadillac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buick" title="Buick">Buick</a> models up to the 1990s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Since 1983 GM and <a href="/wiki/Al-Monsour_Automotive" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Monsour Automotive">Al-Monsour Automotive Company</a> have owned <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Egypt" title="General Motors Egypt">General Motors Egypt</a>, which is currently the only manufacturer of traditional GM branded vehicles in Egypt.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Following the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Anti-Apartheid_Act" title="Comprehensive Anti-Apartheid Act">Comprehensive Anti-Apartheid Act</a> in 1986, GM was forced to divest from South Africa, and GMSA became the independent Delta Motor Corporation. GM purchased a 49% stake in Delta in 1997 following the end of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, and acquired the remaining 51% in 2004, reverting the company to its original name. The company began operating in South Africa in 1913 through its wholly owned subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_South_Africa" title="General Motors South Africa">General Motors South Africa</a>. By 2014 it was targeting the production of 50,000 cars a year but was being hampered by national labour unrest, strikes and protests.<sup id="cite_ref-GMsouthafrica_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMsouthafrica-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another manufacturing base of the GM for the African markets is the <a href="/wiki/Industries_M%C3%A9caniques_Maghr%C3%A9bines" title="Industries Mécaniques Maghrébines">Industries Mécaniques Maghrébines</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">Kairouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, which assembles Isuzu and Mazda models for the Maghreb region. General Motors East Africa (GMEA) located in <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, Kenya assembles a wide range of Isuzu trucks and buses including the popular Isuzu N-Series versatile light commercial vehicle, TF Series pick-ups and Isuzu bus chassis. Formed in 1975, GMEA's facility is the largest assembler of commercial vehicles in the region exporting to East and Central African countries including <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, Tanzania, <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, Rwanda and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>. In addition to assembly, GMEA also markets the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> products <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Spark" title="Chevrolet Spark">Spark</a> and Optra.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the 1920s <i>Miller Brothers Nigeria</i> was founded as an importer of commercial vehicles of the Bedford brand into the country. In 1949, the company opened its own assembly plant and operated under the name <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>/<a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> Motors. In 1965 the plant and its distribution network was split into different companies and renamed as Federated Motors Industries. In 1991 the company was taken in by a joint venture between <b>General Motors</b> and UACN of <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> GM has been represented by the <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a> brand since 1948, GM having acquired the company in 1931. In 2012, GM <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> cars began to be imported into Australia as a niche marque under their own brand name.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> However, as of August 2013, GM has made the decision to remove the Opel brand from Australia noting poor adoption and sales.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In New Zealand GM was represented by Chevrolet, Pontiac and Vauxhall cars all locally-assembled since 1926. Fully imported Holdens appeared in 1954, NZ assembly of Holdens begun in 1957 was slowly phased in through the early 1960s to replace most Vauxhall and all Chevrolet cars. Thirty years ahead of Australia tariff protection was removed and local assembly plants closed in 1984 and 1990. GM became a national sales company and a parts distribution centre.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the early 1990s <a href="/wiki/Holden_New_Zealand" title="Holden New Zealand">General Motors New Zealand</a> did sell a few Isuzu and Opel cars rebranded Holdens in 1994 when New Zealand's GM was renamed Holden.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 10, 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-GM-newsrelease_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-newsrelease-83">[83]</a></sup> GM announced that Holden would cease engine and vehicle manufacturing operations in Australia by the end of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-OZ-manu-end-2017_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OZ-manu-end-2017-84">[84]</a></sup> Beyond 2017 Holden's Australian presence will consist of: a national sales company, a parts distribution centre and, a global design studio.<sup id="cite_ref-GM-newsrelease_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-newsrelease-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsports">Motorsports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=General_Motors&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Motorsports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
